        }

          width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Continuing our discussion from 



<span class="line"><!---->Continuing our discussion from <!----></span>





Issue 1282006



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1282006" title="Heap-use-after-free in FeedbackData::SendReport()"><!---->Issue 1282006<!----></a>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





here, since this is a canonical bug now.



<span class="line"><!---->here, since this is a canonical bug now.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





from 



<span class="line"><!---->from <!----></span>





https://crbug.com/1282006#c12



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1282006#c12" title="Heap-use-after-free in FeedbackData::SendReport()"><!---->https://crbug.com/1282006#c12<!----></a>





:



<span class="line"><!---->:<!----></span>



<br>





> It is normal that FeedbackData outlives the dialog for after the user sends a report, the dialog will be closed shortly. The backend may need to gather more logs before uploading the data and thus may take some time. So yes, a better solution may be to reject the submit request in the first place if the profile used to open the feedback UI has been deleted. The question is how to detect the profile change? 



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; It is normal that FeedbackData outlives the dialog for after the user sends a report, the dialog will be closed shortly. The backend may need to gather more logs before uploading the data and thus may take some time. So yes, a better solution may be to reject the submit request in the first place if the profile used to open the feedback UI has been deleted. The question is how to detect the profile change? <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If FeedbackDialog is the last think that keeps a Profile alive (i.e there are no other browser windows from this profile), you might run into this risk quite often, since the profile will be destroyed as soon as the dialog is closed.



<span class="line"><!---->If FeedbackDialog is the last think that keeps a Profile alive (i.e there are no other browser windows from this profile), you might run into this risk quite often, since the profile will be destroyed as soon as the dialog is closed.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





There have been a recent discussion about how to organize the code that depends on Profile* [1] (sorry, Google-internal links). I think [2] provides an excellent list of recommendations. In general, it is not recommended to observe Profile lifetime directly (though, it's possible through ProfileObserver). There are usually better ways.



<span class="line"><!---->There have been a recent discussion about how to organize the code that depends on Profile* [1] (sorry, Google-internal links). I think [2] provides an excellent list of recommendations. In general, it is not recommended to observe Profile lifetime directly (though, it's possible through ProfileObserver). There are usually better ways.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In your case, FeedbackData depends on a FeedbackUploader and not on a Profile* itself. Weak pointer (



<span class="line"><!---->In your case, FeedbackData depends on a FeedbackUploader and not on a Profile* itself. Weak pointer (<!----></span>





https://crrev.com/c/3347697



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/c/3347697"><!---->https://crrev.com/c/3347697<!----></a>





)



<span class="line"><!---->)<!----></span>





 already eliminates the risk of UaF. FeedbackData might be more proactive and cancel all running tasks as soon as FeedbackUploader is destroyed. This can be implemented by exposing observer methods from FeedbackUploader and subscribing FeedbackData to observe FeedbackUploader.



<span class="line"><!----> already eliminates the risk of UaF. FeedbackData might be more proactive and cancel all running tasks as soon as FeedbackUploader is destroyed. This can be implemented by exposing observer methods from FeedbackUploader and subscribing FeedbackData to observe FeedbackUploader.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[1] 



<span class="line"><!---->[1] <!----></span>





https://groups.google.com/a/google.com/g/chromium-dev-internal/c/EM963SZmgrs/m/oKF79EkzAAAJ



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://groups.google.com/a/google.com/g/chromium-dev-internal/c/EM963SZmgrs/m/oKF79EkzAAAJ"><!---->https://groups.google.com/a/google.com/g/chromium-dev-internal/c/EM963SZmgrs/m/oKF79EkzAAAJ<!----></a>



<br>





[2] 



<span class="line"><!---->[2] <!----></span>





https://groups.google.com/a/google.com/g/chromium-dev-internal/c/EM963SZmgrs/m/6Br0HAs_AAAJ



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://groups.google.com/a/google.com/g/chromium-dev-internal/c/EM963SZmgrs/m/6Br0HAs_AAAJ"><!---->https://groups.google.com/a/google.com/g/chromium-dev-internal/c/EM963SZmgrs/m/6Br0HAs_AAAJ<!----></a>

commit 



<span class="line"><!---->commit <!----></span>





6b080f05f59dbf5ef53fafed634de2ec0bf4fb8e



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/6b080f05f59dbf5ef53fafed634de2ec0bf4fb8e"><!---->6b080f05f59dbf5ef53fafed634de2ec0bf4fb8e<!----></a>



<br>





Author: xiangdong kong <



<span class="line"><!---->Author: xiangdong kong &lt;<!----></span>





xiangdongkong@google.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="/u/xiangdongkong@google.com"><!---->xiangdongkong@google.com<!----></a>





>



<span class="line"><!---->&gt;<!----></span>



<br>





Date: Wed Dec 29 00:08:37 2021



<span class="line"><!---->Date: Wed Dec 29 00:08:37 2021<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





change feedback uploader member in feedback data from raw_ptr to weakptr



<span class="line"><!---->change feedback uploader member in feedback data from raw_ptr to weakptr<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is to fix the security-related heap-use-after-free issue that



<span class="line"><!---->This is to fix the security-related heap-use-after-free issue that<!----></span>



<br>





occurs in the following scenario:



<span class="line"><!---->occurs in the following scenario:<!----></span>



<br>





1) Open the feedback app, enter some description



<span class="line"><!---->1) Open the feedback app, enter some description<!----></span>



<br>





2) Delete existing profile(s)



<span class="line"><!---->2) Delete existing profile(s)<!----></span>



<br>





3) Send the feedback



<span class="line"><!---->3) Send the feedback<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is a bug in the feedback::FeedbackData class which can outlive a



<span class="line"><!---->This is a bug in the feedback::FeedbackData class which can outlive a<!----></span>



<br>





profile while one of its non-owned members, i.e. uploader_, a



<span class="line"><!---->profile while one of its non-owned members, i.e. uploader_, a<!----></span>



<br>





keyedService, gets destroyed with a profile.



<span class="line"><!---->keyedService, gets destroyed with a profile.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The FeedbackData is initialized after user hits "send" to submit a



<span class="line"><!---->The FeedbackData is initialized after user hits "send" to submit a<!----></span>



<br>





report. It is an async process to collect different pieces of data.



<span class="line"><!---->report. It is an async process to collect different pieces of data.<!----></span>



<br>





Since it is not recommended to observe Profile lifetime directly, we can



<span class="line"><!---->Since it is not recommended to observe Profile lifetime directly, we can<!----></span>



<br>





either store the uploader as a weak_ptr or refactor the



<span class="line"><!---->either store the uploader as a weak_ptr or refactor the<!----></span>



<br>





feedback::FeedbackUploader to expose observer method to be subscribed by



<span class="line"><!---->feedback::FeedbackUploader to expose observer method to be subscribed by<!----></span>



<br>





FeedbackData. The latter is way more complex to implement without



<span class="line"><!---->FeedbackData. The latter is way more complex to implement without<!----></span>



<br>





obvious benefit. The scenario is a rare use case too. Therefore, I here



<span class="line"><!---->obvious benefit. The scenario is a rare use case too. Therefore, I here<!----></span>



<br>





choose the weak_ptr approach so that if the uploader_ has been



<span class="line"><!---->choose the weak_ptr approach so that if the uploader_ has been<!----></span>



<br>





destroyed when FeedbackData is about to upload the report, FeedbackData



<span class="line"><!---->destroyed when FeedbackData is about to upload the report, FeedbackData<!----></span>



<br>





will skip calling the uploader_ to upload the report. Thus, the UaF bug



<span class="line"><!---->will skip calling the uploader_ to upload the report. Thus, the UaF bug<!----></span>



<br>





is avoided.



<span class="line"><!---->is avoided.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is not a perfect solution from the user's perspective. Ideally, if



<span class="line"><!---->This is not a perfect solution from the user's perspective. Ideally, if<!----></span>



<br>





the feedback app is opened with a profile, and then the profile is



<span class="line"><!---->the feedback app is opened with a profile, and then the profile is<!----></span>



<br>





deleted, the app should be closed or notify the user that it should be



<span class="line"><!---->deleted, the app should be closed or notify the user that it should be<!----></span>



<br>





reopened in order to send a report due to profile change. But this is a



<span class="line"><!---->reopened in order to send a report due to profile change. But this is a<!----></span>



<br>





rare case and outside of the scope.



<span class="line"><!---->rare case and outside of the scope.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.
